{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01WUVmjd2j5yzQui5vLEANsw","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_017AK7qGQfiVBbBLr4QkAiaW","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\nThis document provides comprehensive API documentation for Cilium's eBPF map API in the `pkg/bpf` package. It serves as a complete reference for developers working with eBPF maps in Cilium.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Core Concepts](#core-concepts)\n2. [Map Type and Creation](#map-type-and-creation)\n3. [Map Lifecycle](#map-lifecycle)\n4. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n5. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n6. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n7. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n8. [Event System](#event-system)\n9. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n10. [Usage Examples](#usage-examples)\n\n---\n\n## Core Concepts\n\n### Design Philosophy\n\nCilium's eBPF map API provides type-safe Go wrappers around kernel eBPF maps. The API emphasizes:\n\n- **Type Safety**: Keys and values must implement `MapKey` and `MapValue` interfaces\n- **Lifecycle Management**: Maps have explicit creation, opening, and closing semantics\n- **Persistence**: Maps can be pinned to the BPF filesystem for reuse across process restarts\n- **Synchronization**: Optional cache tracking ensures consistency between userspace and kernel\n- **Event Streaming**: Built-in event buffer for auditing map operations\n\n### Supported Map Types\n\nThe API supports the following eBPF map types via `ebpf.MapType`:\n\n- `Hash`: Standard hash map\n- `Array`: Fixed-size array\n- `PerCPUHash`: Per-CPU hash map\n- `PerCPUArray`: Per-CPU array\n- `LRUHash`: LRU eviction hash map\n- `LRUCPUHash`: LRU per-CPU hash map\n- `LPMTrie`: Longest prefix match trie\n- `RingBuffer`: Ring buffer for events\n- `ProgramArray`: Program arrays for tail calls\n- `PerCPUCGroupStorage`: Per-CPU cgroup storage\n\n---\n\n## Map Type and Creation\n\n### The Map Struct\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    // Logger for map operations\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // ... (private fields)\n}\n```\n\nThe `Map` struct represents a user-space handle to a kernel eBPF map. It manages lifecycle, synchronization, and optional caching.\n\n### Creating a New Map\n\n#### NewMap\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new `Map` instance configured with the given parameters.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: Map basename (not a full path). Used for logging and as the basis for the pin path.\n- `mapType`: The eBPF map type (e.g., `ebpf.Hash`)\n- `mapKey`: A zero-initialized instance of your key type that implements `MapKey`\n- `mapValue`: A zero-initialized instance of your value type that implements `MapValue`\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold\n- `flags`: eBPF map creation flags (e.g., `unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`)\n\n**Returns:** An uninitialized `Map` instance. The map is not yet created in the kernel.\n\n**Behavioral Notes:**\n- The returned `Map` is not opened or created yet. Call `OpenOrCreate()` or `Open()` to bring it into the kernel.\n- The key and value sizes are automatically determined from the struct types using reflection.\n- The map name is derived from the base filename of the `name` parameter.\n\n#### NewMapWithInnerSpec\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey,\n    mapValue MapValue, maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new `Map` with an inner map specification, used for maps-of-maps and programs-of-programs.\n\n### Opening and Creating Maps\n\n#### OpenOrCreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open an existing pinned map, or creates a new one if it doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If a map is already pinned at the computed path, opens it\n- If the pinned map's attributes (type, key/value size, capacity, flags) differ from the `Map`'s configuration, **deletes the old map and creates a new one** with the current configuration\n- If no pinned map exists, creates and pins a new one\n- Non-persistent maps (marked as such) are always recreated\n\n**Returns:** `nil` on success, or an error if the operation fails.\n\n**Side Effects:**\n- Creates the map in the kernel (or reuses an existing one)\n- Pins the map to the BPF filesystem if attributes match or the map was newly created\n- Sets the internal map handle, making subsequent operations functional\n\n#### Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens an already-pinned map from the filesystem without creating it.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Loads a previously pinned map from its computed path\n- Fails with an error if the map does not exist\n\n**Returns:** `nil` on success, `os.ErrNotExist` if the pinned map is not found, or another error on failure.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- When you're certain the map already exists and was pinned by a previous instance\n- For reading-only operations on long-lived maps\n\n#### CreateUnpinned\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates a map in the kernel **without pinning it** to the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates the map in the kernel only\n- Does not pin the map, so it will be lost when the process exits\n- Cannot be reused by subsequent processes\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Temporary maps with short lifespans\n- Maps that don't need to persist across restarts\n\n#### Create\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nSimilar to `OpenOrCreate()`, but closes the map immediately after creating or opening it.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `OpenOrCreate()` followed by `Close()`\n- Useful for setup operations that don't require the map to remain open\n\n#### Recreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves any existing pin and recreates the map from scratch.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the pinned map at the computed path (if it exists)\n- Creates a new map in the kernel\n- Pins the new map\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Force-refreshing a map that may have been corrupted\n- Resetting a map to a clean state\n\n**Preconditions:**\n- The map must not already be open (`IsOpen()` must return `false`)\n\n---\n\n## Map Lifecycle\n\n### Checking Map State\n\n#### IsOpen\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\nReturns `true` if the map has been opened/created in the kernel.\n\n### Closing Maps\n\n#### Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map handle, releasing kernel resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Closes the underlying eBPF map handle\n- If cache synchronization is enabled, cancels any pending error resolver controllers\n- Unregisters the map from internal tracking\n- Does not unpin the map from the filesystem\n\n**Important:** After calling `Close()`, you can call `Open()` again to reopen the map.\n\n### File Descriptor Access\n\n#### FD\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int\n```\n\nReturns the raw file descriptor for the underlying eBPF map.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Direct syscall interactions\n- Integration with libraries expecting raw FDs\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup (Read)\n\n#### Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nRetrieves a value by key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Returns a **new instance** of the value type with the data from the kernel\n- Safe to retain the returned value; no shared references\n\n**Returns:**\n- The value associated with the key, or\n- An error (typically `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if the key is not in the map)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nvalue, err := myMap.Lookup(key)\nif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n    // Key not found\n} else if err != nil {\n    // Other error\n}\n```\n\n### Update (Write)\n\n#### Update\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates a key-value pair in the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- If a cache is enabled, tracks the entry with status `OK` on success\n- If a cache is enabled and the update fails, tracks the entry with status `Insert` (pending retry) and schedules an error resolver controller\n- Emits a `MapUpdate` event to the event buffer if enabled\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails (e.g., out of memory).\n\n**Synchronization Details:**\n- If cache is enabled and the update fails, an error resolver controller is scheduled to periodically retry the update\n- The cache entry records the desired action, actual value, and last error\n- This allows graceful recovery from transient failures\n\n### Delete (Remove)\n\n#### Delete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes a key-value pair from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires a write lock (serializes with other operations)\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- If the key doesn't exist, returns an error (typically `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`)\n- If a cache is enabled, removes the entry on success or marks it with status `Delete` (pending retry) on failure\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails.\n\n#### SilentDelete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nDeletes a key from the map, silently ignoring `ErrKeyNotExist` errors.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns `(false, nil)` if the key doesn't exist\n- Returns `(true, nil)` if deletion succeeded\n- Returns `(false, err)` for other errors\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Cleanup operations where it's OK if the entry was already gone\n- NAT GC where entries may have already been reclaimed\n\n#### DeleteLocked\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes a key from the map when the map lock is already held.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- **Must only be called from within a `DumpCallback`** to avoid deadlocks\n- Assumes `m.lock` is already acquired for writing\n- Uses the internal `delete()` method which updates cache and events\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Conditional cleanup during iteration (e.g., remove expired entries during a dump)\n\n**Preconditions:**\n- Must be called from within a callback passed to `DumpWithCallback()` or similar iteration methods\n- These callbacks receive the lock already acquired\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := myMap.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    if isExpired(value) {\n        // Safe to delete from within callback\n        myMap.DeleteLocked(key)\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### Batch Operations\n\n#### BatchLookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any,\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)\n```\n\nPerforms a batch lookup using the eBPF batch API.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cursor`: State tracker for the batch operation, maintained across calls\n- `keysOut`: Slice of keys to populate\n- `valuesOut`: Slice of values to populate\n- `opts`: Optional batch options\n\n**Returns:** The number of elements retrieved, and an error (possibly `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` when done, or `unix.ENOSPC` if the buffer is too small).\n\n**Note:** Use `BatchIterator` for a more convenient API that handles retries and buffer resizing automatically.\n\n#### BatchCount\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nCounts the total number of elements in the map using batch lookups.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works for hash, LRU-hash, and LPM-trie maps\n- Handles `unix.ENOSPC` errors by doubling the buffer size and retrying (up to 3 times)\n- Returns the total count or an error\n\n**Note:** For maps that don't fit the supported types, returns an error.\n\n#### DeleteAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and deleting individually.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires a write lock\n- Iterates through all keys and deletes each one\n- If cache is enabled, marks all entries as pending deletion before iteration\n- Updates entries in the cache as deletion succeeds or fails\n- Emits a `MapDeleteAll` event to the event buffer if enabled\n\n**Important:** Entries added to the map during this operation may survive the deletion.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Complete map reset when reloading policies\n- Cleanup before map recreation\n\n#### ClearAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nClears all entries by updating them to their zero values instead of deleting.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Cannot be used with maps that have events buffer or value cache enabled\n- Iterates through all keys and updates each to an empty/zero value\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- When you need to preserve map structure but clear contents\n- Some kernel subsystems require this pattern instead of deletion\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### Simple Iteration with Callbacks\n\n#### DumpWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all map entries and calls the callback for each one.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a read lock\n- Creates fresh instances of key and value types for each callback invocation\n- Safe to retain the values received in the callback (they're not shared references)\n\n**Returns:** An error if iteration fails.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := myMap.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", key, value)\n})\n```\n\n**Important:** Do not call map mutation methods (Update, Delete) from the callback without using `DeleteLocked()`. The lock is held as a read lock, not write.\n\n#### DumpWithCallbackIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback()`, but returns silently if the map doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if the map's pinned file exists first\n- If it doesn't exist, returns `nil` without calling the callback\n- Otherwise behaves like `DumpWithCallback()`\n\n### Per-CPU Iteration\n\n#### DumpPerCPUWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over a per-CPU map and calls the callback with all per-CPU values at once.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- The value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue` interface\n- The callback receives a slice of values (one per CPU)\n- Each callback invocation gets fresh value slices\n\n**Preconditions:**\n- The map must be a per-CPU map type (PerCPUHash, PerCPUArray, etc.)\n- The value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := myPerCPUMap.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    valuesSlice := values.(*[]MyValue)\n    // Process per-CPU values\n})\n```\n\n### Reliable Iteration with Position Tracking\n\n#### DumpReliablyWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nIterates over a map with advanced tracking to handle concurrent modifications.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Maintains tracking of previously seen keys to recover from iterator resets\n- If a key is deleted during iteration, backtracks to the previous key and resumes from there\n- Caps maximum iterations at 4x the map's max entries to prevent infinite loops\n- Updates the `DumpStats` object with iteration statistics\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function called for each entry\n- `stats`: A `DumpStats` object (created via `NewDumpStats(m)`) for tracking statistics\n\n**Returns:**\n- `nil` if iteration completes successfully\n- `ErrMaxLookup` if the iteration limit is exceeded (indicates a very unstable map)\n- Other errors if iteration fails\n\n**Statistics Provided:**\n- `Lookup`: Total number of key lookups performed\n- `LookupFailed`: Number of failed lookups (key was deleted)\n- `Interrupted`: Number of times iteration was interrupted by deletion\n- `KeyFallback`: Number of times fallback to previous key was used\n- `Completed`: Whether iteration completed successfully\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- When the map is being modified by other processes during iteration\n- Ensuring complete enumeration despite concurrent updates\n\n### Batch Iterator (Modern API)\n\n#### NewBatchIterator\n\n```go\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nCreates a new batch iterator for type-safe batched iteration.\n\n**Type Parameters:**\n- `KT`: Key type (e.g., `MyKey`)\n- `VT`: Value type (e.g., `MyValue`)\n- `KP`: Key pointer type (must be `*KT` and implement `MapKey`)\n- `VP`: Value pointer type (must be `*VT` and implement `MapValue`)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](myMap)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", *k, *v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    // Handle iteration error\n}\n```\n\n#### IterateAll\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context,\n    opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\nReturns an iterator Seq2 that yields all key-value pairs from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Uses the eBPF batch API for efficient iteration\n- Handles `unix.ENOSPC` errors by automatically doubling the buffer size and retrying (up to 3 times by default)\n- Respects the provided context (stops iteration if context is cancelled)\n- Resets internal state on each call, allowing reuse of the same iterator\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for cancellation\n- `opts`: Optional configuration for the iteration (batch size, retry count, batch options)\n\n**Returns:** An `iter.Seq2[*KT, *VT]` that can be used in `for k, v := range` loops.\n\n**Behavior on Errors:**\n- If iteration fails due to insufficient buffer (ENOSPC), automatically retries with a larger buffer\n- If retries are exhausted, iteration stops and error is available via `Err()`\n- If other errors occur, iteration stops immediately\n\n**Supported Map Types:**\n- Hash, LRUHash, LPMTrie (only)\n\n#### Batch Iterator Options\n\n##### WithMaxRetries\n\n```go\nfunc WithMaxRetries[...](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nSets the maximum number of buffer expansion retries (default: 3).\n\n##### WithStartingChunkSize\n\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[...](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nSets the initial batch size (default: computed from map size).\n\n##### WithEBPFBatchOpts\n\n```go\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[...](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nPasses through eBPF-specific batch options.\n\n#### Err\n\n```go\nfunc (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\nReturns any error encountered during the previous iteration.\n\n**Note:** Error is reset on subsequent calls to `IterateAll()`.\n\n#### CountAll\n\n```go\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)\n```\n\nHelper function that counts all entries by iterating with the batch iterator.\n\n### Simple Dump to Map\n\n#### Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nDumps the entire map into a `map[string][]string`.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates the map using `DumpWithCallback()`\n- Populates the provided map with string representations of keys and values\n- Multiple values per key are stored as a slice\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Exporting map contents for debugging\n- API responses showing map state\n\n#### DumpIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nLike `Dump()`, but returns silently if the map doesn't exist.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Understanding Pinning\n\nPinning is the mechanism Cilium uses to persist eBPF maps to the filesystem so they survive process restarts. When a map is pinned:\n\n1. It's created in the kernel\n2. A reference to it is stored in the BPF filesystem at a specific path\n3. Subsequent processes can open and reuse the pinned map via its path\n\n### Map Paths\n\n#### BPFFSRoot\n\n```go\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n```\n\nReturns the absolute path to the BPF filesystem mount point.\n\n**Default:** `/sys/fs/bpf` (or `/run/cilium/bpffs` if running in a containerized environment without proper host setup)\n\n**Important:** This function locks the BPFFS root and must be called before any other path-related functions.\n\n#### CiliumPath\n\n```go\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n```\n\nReturns the path to the Cilium object directory within the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Returns:** `{BPFFSRoot()}/cilium`\n\n#### TCGlobalsPath\n\n```go\nfunc TCGlobalsPath() string\n```\n\nReturns the path to the TC (traffic control) globals directory.\n\n**Returns:** `{BPFFSRoot()}/tc/globals`\n\n**Note:** Used for legacy map pin paths.\n\n#### MapPath\n\n```go\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n```\n\nReturns the full filesystem path for a map with the given name.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If running in the Cilium agent, returns `{TCGlobalsPath()}/{name}`\n- Otherwise, queries mount info to find the BPF filesystem location\n\n#### LocalMapName\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\nGenerates a map name that's local to a specific ID (e.g., per-endpoint).\n\n**Returns:** `{name}{id:05d}` (e.g., `mymap00001`)\n\n#### LocalMapPath\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\nReturns the path for a map that's local to a specific ID.\n\n### Map Path Methods\n\n#### Path\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\nReturns the computed path where this map is (or will be) pinned.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If the path hasn't been set, computes it from the map name\n- Returns an error if the path cannot be computed\n\n**Returns:** The pinned path, or an error.\n\n#### Name\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n```\n\nReturns the basename of the map.\n\n### Unpin Operations\n\n#### Unpin\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n```\n\nRemoves the map from the BPF filesystem (unpin operation).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Gets the pin path\n- Removes the pinned file/directory\n\n**Important:** This does **not** close the map or release kernel resources. If the map is still open in other processes, it remains in the kernel.\n\n#### UnpinIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\nUnpins the map if it exists, silently succeeding if it doesn't.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if the pinned file exists first\n- Only calls `Unpin()` if it does\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapKey.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String()` for debugging and event logging\n- Must implement `New()` to create fresh instances for iteration\n- Usually a struct with field tags matching eBPF struct layout (e.g., `align` tags)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyKey struct {\n    ID     uint32 `align:\"id\"`\n    Flags  uint8  `align:\"flags\"`\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyKey{ID: %d, Flags: %d}\", k.ID, k.Flags)\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &MyKey{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapValue.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String()` for debugging and event logging\n- Must implement `New()` to create fresh instances for iteration\n- Usually a struct matching eBPF value struct layout\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Count uint64 `align:\"count\"`\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyValue{Count: %d}\", v.Count)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyValue{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs implementing MapValue.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n**Used for:** Per-CPU maps that store separate values for each CPU.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must also implement `MapValue`\n- Must implement `NewSlice()` to create fresh slice instances for iteration\n- The returned slice should be `*[]YourType` where `YourType` implements `MapValue`\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyCPUValue struct {\n    CPUData uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyCPUValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyCPUValue{CPUData: %d}\", v.CPUData)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyCPUValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyCPUValue{}\n}\n\ntype MyCPUValues []MyCPUValue\n\nfunc (v *MyCPUValue) NewSlice() any {\n    return &MyCPUValues{}\n}\n```\n\n### EndpointKey Example\n\nThe `EndpointKey` is a concrete example of a `MapKey` that represents endpoints in Cilium:\n\n```go\nconst (\n    EndpointKeyIPv4 uint8 = 1\n    EndpointKeyIPv6 uint8 = 2\n)\n\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6 `align:\"$union0\"`  // IPv6 (or IPv4 in lowest 4 bytes)\n    Family    uint8      `align:\"family\"`\n    Key       uint8      `align:\"key\"`\n    ClusterID uint16     `align:\"cluster_id\"`\n}\n\nfunc NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {\n    // Constructs an EndpointKey from an IP address\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    // Provides string representation\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\n### Understanding Events\n\nWhen events buffer is enabled, the map tracks all mutation operations (updates and deletes) in a ring buffer. This is useful for:\n\n- Auditing map changes\n- Streaming changes to external systems\n- Debugging map state changes\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n#### WithEvents\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables the event buffer for this map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `c.Enabled`: Whether to enable the buffer\n- `c.MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to store (in-memory)\n- `c.TTL`: Time-to-live for events; older events are garbage collected\n\n**Returns:** The map (for chaining).\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nmyMap.WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n    Enabled: true,\n    MaxSize: 10000,\n    TTL: 5 * time.Minute,\n})\n```\n\n### Event Types\n\n#### Action Enum\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate  Action = iota // Update/Insert operation\n    MapDelete               // Delete operation\n    MapDeleteAll            // Bulk delete operation\n)\n```\n\n### Event Structure\n\n#### Event\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time\n    // (private action field)\n    Key           MapKey\n    Value         MapValue\n    DesiredAction DesiredAction\n    LastError     error\n}\n```\n\n**Fields:**\n- `Timestamp`: When the operation occurred\n- `GetAction()`: Returns the action as a string (\"update\", \"delete\", \"delete-all\")\n- `GetKey()`: Returns the key string representation\n- `GetValue()`: Returns the value string representation (or \"<nil>\" for deletes)\n- `GetLastError()`: Returns any error from the operation\n- `GetDesiredAction()`: Returns the desired action status (OK, Insert, Delete)\n\n### Event Subscription\n\n#### DumpAndSubscribe\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool) void\n```\n\nDumps existing events and optionally subscribes to future ones.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for the subscription (cancel to stop receiving events)\n- `callback`: Function called for each event (existing and future)\n- `follow`: If `true`, continues receiving events; if `false`, only dumps existing\n\n**Behavior:**\n- First, calls the callback with all existing events in the buffer (in order)\n- If `follow` is `true`, subscribes to future events and calls callback for each new one\n- Uses the provided context for lifetime management\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nmyMap.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(event Event) {\n    if event.GetAction() == \"update\" {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Updated: %s = %s\\n\", event.GetKey(), event.GetValue())\n    }\n}, true) // Follow = true for streaming\n\n// Subscription continues until ctx is cancelled\n```\n\n#### IsEventsEnabled\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nReturns whether event buffering is enabled for this map.\n\n### Desired Action Status\n\nThe `DesiredAction` field tracks the state of an entry:\n\n```go\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is in sync with kernel\n    Insert                       // Entry needs to be inserted (pending retry)\n    Delete                       // Entry needs to be deleted (pending retry)\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\n### Loading eBPF Collections\n\nThe collection loading API handles loading compiled eBPF ELF files (collections of programs and maps) into the kernel.\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants to substitute in eBPF code\n    Constants any\n\n    // Map renames: map old names to new names\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Maps to substitute (already-open maps)\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to dump configuration constants\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n### LoadAndAssign\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF collection from a spec and assigns programs/maps to fields in a struct.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for operations\n- `to`: A struct with fields for eBPF programs and maps (uses `ebpf` struct tags)\n- `spec`: The compiled eBPF collection spec\n- `opts`: Configuration for loading\n\n**Returns:**\n- A commit function to call after programs are attached to kernel hooks\n- An error if loading fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Analyzes struct fields to determine what to load\n- Loads the collection into the kernel\n- Assigns loaded programs and maps to the provided struct\n- Returns a function that must be called after entrypoints are attached (for final pinning)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype Objects struct {\n    ProgIngress *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_to_netdev\"`\n    ProgEgress  *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_from_netdev\"`\n    MapState    *Map          `ebpf:\"cilium_state\"`\n}\n\nobjs := &Objects{}\ncommit, err := LoadAndAssign(logger, objs, spec, nil)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Attach programs to hooks\n// ...\n\n// Commit pending map pins after attachment\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### LoadCollection\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads a collection spec into the kernel with advanced options.\n\n**Returns:**\n- The loaded collection\n- A commit function for pending map pins\n- An error if loading fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Applies constants to the spec\n- Renames maps as specified\n- Performs reachability analysis to prune unused code\n- Resolves tail call slots\n- Handles incompatible pinned maps by recreating them\n- Returns a commit function to finalize pinning after program attachment\n\n**Important:** The commit function **must** be called after all programs are attached to kernel hooks to ensure pending map pins are finalized.\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Map Creation and CRUD\n\n```go\npackage main\n\nimport (\n    \"fmt\"\n    \"log/slog\"\n\n    \"github.com/cilium/ebpf\"\n    \"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/bpf\"\n)\n\ntype Counter struct {\n    ID uint32 `align:\"id\"`\n}\n\nfunc (c *Counter) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"id=%d\", c.ID)\n}\n\nfunc (c *Counter) New() bpf.MapKey {\n    return &Counter{}\n}\n\ntype Count struct {\n    Value uint64 `align:\"value\"`\n}\n\nfunc (c *Count) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"count=%d\", c.Value)\n}\n\nfunc (c *Count) New() bpf.MapValue {\n    return &Count{}\n}\n\nfunc main() {\n    logger := slog.Default()\n\n    // Initialize BPF filesystem\n    bpf.CheckOrMountFS(logger, \"\")\n\n    // Create a map\n    m := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_counters\",\n        ebpf.Hash,\n        &Counter{},\n        &Count{},\n        1000,\n        0)\n\n    // Open or create the map in the kernel\n    if err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to create map\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n    defer m.Close()\n\n    // Update a value\n    key := &Counter{ID: 42}\n    value := &Count{Value: 100}\n    if err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to update\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n\n    // Lookup a value\n    result, err := m.Lookup(key)\n    if err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to lookup\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n    fmt.Printf(\"Result: %v\\n\", result)\n\n    // Delete a value\n    if err := m.Delete(key); err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to delete\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Iteration with BatchIterator\n\n```go\nfunc dumpMapContents(ctx context.Context, m *bpf.Map) error {\n    iter := bpf.NewBatchIterator[Counter, Count](m)\n\n    for k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", k, v)\n    }\n\n    if err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n        return fmt.Errorf(\"iteration failed: %w\", err)\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n### Conditional Deletion During Iteration\n\n```go\nfunc deleteExpiredEntries(m *bpf.Map) error {\n    return m.DumpWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n        if isExpired(value) {\n            // Safe to delete within callback using DeleteLocked\n            if err := m.DeleteLocked(key); err != nil {\n                // Log error but continue iteration\n                fmt.Printf(\"Failed to delete: %v\\n\", err)\n            }\n        }\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### Event Subscription\n\n```go\nfunc subscribeToMapChanges(ctx context.Context, m *bpf.Map) {\n    m.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(event bpf.Event) {\n        action := event.GetAction()\n        key := event.GetKey()\n        value := event.GetValue()\n\n        fmt.Printf(\"[%s] %s = %s\\n\", action, key, value)\n\n        if err := event.GetLastError(); err != nil {\n            fmt.Printf(\"  Error: %v\\n\", err)\n        }\n    }, true) // follow=true for streaming\n}\n```\n\n### Per-CPU Map Usage\n\n```go\ntype PerCPUStats struct {\n    PacketCount uint64 `align:\"pkt_count\"`\n}\n\nfunc (s *PerCPUStats) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"pkts=%d\", s.PacketCount)\n}\n\nfunc (s *PerCPUStats) New() bpf.MapValue {\n    return &PerCPUStats{}\n}\n\ntype PerCPUStatsSlice []PerCPUStats\n\nfunc (s *PerCPUStats) NewSlice() any {\n    return &PerCPUStatsSlice{}\n}\n\nfunc dumpPerCPUStats(m *bpf.Map) error {\n    return m.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, values any) {\n        statsSlice := values.(*PerCPUStatsSlice)\n        for cpu, stats := range *statsSlice {\n            fmt.Printf(\"CPU %d: %v\\n\", cpu, stats)\n        }\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### Map with Cache and Error Recovery\n\n```go\nfunc createManagedMap() *bpf.Map {\n    return bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_managed\",\n        ebpf.Hash,\n        &Counter{},\n        &Count{},\n        10000,\n        0).\n        WithCache(). // Enable cache for consistency tracking\n        WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n            Enabled: true,\n            MaxSize: 5000,\n            TTL: 10 * time.Minute,\n        })\n}\n```\n\n### Reliable Iteration with Statistics\n\n```go\nfunc dumpReliably(m *bpf.Map) error {\n    stats := bpf.NewDumpStats(m)\n\n    err := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n        fmt.Printf(\"%v: %v\\n\", key, value)\n    }, stats)\n\n    if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, bpf.ErrMaxLookup) {\n        return err\n    }\n\n    fmt.Printf(\"Lookups: %d, Failed: %d, Interrupted: %d\\n\",\n        stats.Lookup, stats.LookupFailed, stats.Interrupted)\n\n    if stats.Completed {\n        fmt.Println(\"Iteration completed successfully\")\n    }\n\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Concepts\n\n### Cache and Synchronization\n\nWhen `.WithCache()` is enabled:\n\n- All entries updated by userspace are tracked in a local cache\n- Each entry records its desired action (`OK`, `Insert`, `Delete`) and last error\n- On update failure, the cache is marked for synchronization\n- An error resolver controller periodically retries failed operations\n- This ensures eventual consistency between userspace and kernel state\n\n### Pressure Metrics\n\nMaps can be configured to report \"pressure\" (capacity usage):\n\n```go\nm.WithPressureMetric(registry)  // Report with 0% threshold\nm.WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry, 0.8)  // Report when > 80% full\n```\n\nThe pressure metric tracks: `(cache_size / max_entries)`\n\n### Map Registration\n\nMaps are automatically registered and tracked internally for debugging. Use `GetModel()` to retrieve the API representation:\n\n```go\nmodel := m.GetModel()  // Returns *models.BPFMap with cache entries\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Types\n\n- `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`: Key not found in map\n- `ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible`: Existing map has different attributes\n- `unix.ENOSPC`: Batch lookup buffer too small (auto-retried by BatchIterator)\n- `os.ErrNotExist`: Pinned map file doesn't exist\n- `ErrMaxLookup`: Iteration limit reached (concurrent modifications)\n\n### Best Practices\n\n1. **Always check errors** from `Lookup()` with `errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)`\n2. **Use `SilentDelete()`** for cleanup operations where missing entries are OK\n3. **Call `Close()`** in defer statements to ensure resources are released\n4. **Enable cache** for maps with complex synchronization requirements\n5. **Use `DumpReliablyWithCallback()`** when iterating maps that may be modified concurrently\n6. **Use `BatchIterator`** for efficient iteration of large maps\n\n---\n\n## See Also\n\n- eBPF kernel documentation: https://docs.kernel.org/userspace-api/ebpf/index.html\n- Cilium documentation: https://docs.cilium.io\n- ebpf-go library: https://github.com/cilium/ebpf\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3456,"cache_read_input_tokens":60147,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3456},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e31125d2-f8b7-4eae-8178-a33aede3aea9","uuid":"ba0d80a6-ebe8-4127-b398-3c600d535191"}

It serves as a complete reference for developers working with eBPF maps in Cilium.\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Core Concepts](#core-concepts)\n2. [Map Type and Creation](#map-type-and-creation)\n3. [Map Lifecycle](#map-lifecycle)\n4. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n5. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n6. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n7. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n8. [Event System](#event-system)\n9. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n10. [Usage Examples](#usage-examples)\n\n---\n\n## Core Concepts\n\n### Design Philosophy\n\nCilium's eBPF map API provides type-safe Go wrappers around kernel eBPF maps. The API emphasizes:\n\n- **Type Safety**: Keys and values must implement `MapKey` and `MapValue` interfaces\n- **Lifecycle Management**: Maps have explicit creation, opening, and closing semantics\n- **Persistence**: Maps can be pinned to the BPF filesystem for reuse across process restarts\n- **Synchronization**: Optional cache tracking ensures consistency between userspace and kernel\n- **Event Streaming**: Built-in event buffer for auditing map operations\n\n### Supported Map Types\n\nThe API supports the following eBPF map types via `ebpf.MapType`:\n\n- `Hash`: Standard hash map\n- `Array`: Fixed-size array\n- `PerCPUHash`: Per-CPU hash map\n- `PerCPUArray`: Per-CPU array\n- `LRUHash`: LRU eviction hash map\n- `LRUCPUHash`: LRU per-CPU hash map\n- `LPMTrie`: Longest prefix match trie\n- `RingBuffer`: Ring buffer for events\n- `ProgramArray`: Program arrays for tail calls\n- `PerCPUCGroupStorage`: Per-CPU cgroup storage\n\n---\n\n## Map Type and Creation\n\n### The Map Struct\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    // Logger for map operations\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // ... (private fields)\n}\n```\n\nThe `Map` struct represents a user-space handle to a kernel eBPF map. It manages lifecycle, synchronization, and optional caching.\n\n### Creating a New Map\n\n#### NewMap\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new `Map` instance configured with the given parameters.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: Map basename (not a full path). Used for logging and as the basis for the pin path.\n- `mapType`: The eBPF map type (e.g., `ebpf.Hash`)\n- `mapKey`: A zero-initialized instance of your key type that implements `MapKey`\n- `mapValue`: A zero-initialized instance of your value type that implements `MapValue`\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold\n- `flags`: eBPF map creation flags (e.g., `unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`)\n\n**Returns:** An uninitialized `Map` instance. The map is not yet created in the kernel.\n\n**Behavioral Notes:**\n- The returned `Map` is not opened or created yet. Call `OpenOrCreate()` or `Open()` to bring it into the kernel.\n- The key and value sizes are automatically determined from the struct types using reflection.\n- The map name is derived from the base filename of the `name` parameter.\n\n#### NewMapWithInnerSpec\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey,\n    mapValue MapValue, maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\nCreates a new `Map` with an inner map specification, used for maps-of-maps and programs-of-programs.\n\n### Opening and Creating Maps\n\n#### OpenOrCreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open an existing pinned map, or creates a new one if it doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If a map is already pinned at the computed path, opens it\n- If the pinned map's attributes (type, key/value size, capacity, flags) differ from the `Map`'s configuration, **deletes the old map and creates a new one** with the current configuration\n- If no pinned map exists, creates and pins a new one\n- Non-persistent maps (marked as such) are always recreated\n\n**Returns:** `nil` on success, or an error if the operation fails.\n\n**Side Effects:**\n- Creates the map in the kernel (or reuses an existing one)\n- Pins the map to the BPF filesystem if attributes match or the map was newly created\n- Sets the internal map handle, making subsequent operations functional\n\n#### Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens an already-pinned map from the filesystem without creating it.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Loads a previously pinned map from its computed path\n- Fails with an error if the map does not exist\n\n**Returns:** `nil` on success, `os.ErrNotExist` if the pinned map is not found, or another error on failure.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- When you're certain the map already exists and was pinned by a previous instance\n- For reading-only operations on long-lived maps\n\n#### CreateUnpinned\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates a map in the kernel **without pinning it** to the filesystem.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates the map in the kernel only\n- Does not pin the map, so it will be lost when the process exits\n- Cannot be reused by subsequent processes\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Temporary maps with short lifespans\n- Maps that don't need to persist across restarts\n\n#### Create\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nSimilar to `OpenOrCreate()`, but closes the map immediately after creating or opening it.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `OpenOrCreate()` followed by `Close()`\n- Useful for setup operations that don't require the map to remain open\n\n#### Recreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves any existing pin and recreates the map from scratch.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Removes the pinned map at the computed path (if it exists)\n- Creates a new map in the kernel\n- Pins the new map\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Force-refreshing a map that may have been corrupted\n- Resetting a map to a clean state\n\n**Preconditions:**\n- The map must not already be open (`IsOpen()` must return `false`)\n\n---\n\n## Map Lifecycle\n\n### Checking Map State\n\n#### IsOpen\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\nReturns `true` if the map has been opened/created in the kernel.\n\n### Closing Maps\n\n#### Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map handle, releasing kernel resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Closes the underlying eBPF map handle\n- If cache synchronization is enabled, cancels any pending error resolver controllers\n- Unregisters the map from internal tracking\n- Does not unpin the map from the filesystem\n\n**Important:** After calling `Close()`, you can call `Open()` again to reopen the map.\n\n### File Descriptor Access\n\n#### FD\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int\n```\n\nReturns the raw file descriptor for the underlying eBPF map.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Direct syscall interactions\n- Integration with libraries expecting raw FDs\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup (Read)\n\n#### Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nRetrieves a value by key from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Returns a **new instance** of the value type with the data from the kernel\n- Safe to retain the returned value; no shared references\n\n**Returns:**\n- The value associated with the key, or\n- An error (typically `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` if the key is not in the map)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nkey := &MyKey{ID: 42}\nvalue, err := myMap.Lookup(key)\nif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n    // Key not found\n} else if err != nil {\n    // Other error\n}\n```\n\n### Update (Write)\n\n#### Update\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates a key-value pair in the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- If a cache is enabled, tracks the entry with status `OK` on success\n- If a cache is enabled and the update fails, tracks the entry with status `Insert` (pending retry) and schedules an error resolver controller\n- Emits a `MapUpdate` event to the event buffer if enabled\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails (e.g., out of memory).\n\n**Synchronization Details:**\n- If cache is enabled and the update fails, an error resolver controller is scheduled to periodically retry the update\n- The cache entry records the desired action, actual value, and last error\n- This allows graceful recovery from transient failures\n\n### Delete (Remove)\n\n#### Delete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes a key-value pair from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires a write lock (serializes with other operations)\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- If the key doesn't exist, returns an error (typically `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`)\n- If a cache is enabled, removes the entry on success or marks it with status `Delete` (pending retry) on failure\n\n**Returns:** An error if the operation fails.\n\n#### SilentDelete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nDeletes a key from the map, silently ignoring `ErrKeyNotExist` errors.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns `(false, nil)` if the key doesn't exist\n- Returns `(true, nil)` if deletion succeeded\n- Returns `(false, err)` for other errors\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Cleanup operations where it's OK if the entry was already gone\n- NAT GC where entries may have already been reclaimed\n\n#### DeleteLocked\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes a key from the map when the map lock is already held.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- **Must only be called from within a `DumpCallback`** to avoid deadlocks\n- Assumes `m.lock` is already acquired for writing\n- Uses the internal `delete()` method which updates cache and events\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Conditional cleanup during iteration (e.g., remove expired entries during a dump)\n\n**Preconditions:**\n- Must be called from within a callback passed to `DumpWithCallback()` or similar iteration methods\n- These callbacks receive the lock already acquired\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := myMap.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    if isExpired(value) {\n        // Safe to delete from within callback\n        myMap.DeleteLocked(key)\n    }\n})\n```\n\n### Batch Operations\n\n#### BatchLookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any,\n    opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)\n```\n\nPerforms a batch lookup using the eBPF batch API.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cursor`: State tracker for the batch operation, maintained across calls\n- `keysOut`: Slice of keys to populate\n- `valuesOut`: Slice of values to populate\n- `opts`: Optional batch options\n\n**Returns:** The number of elements retrieved, and an error (possibly `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` when done, or `unix.ENOSPC` if the buffer is too small).\n\n**Note:** Use `BatchIterator` for a more convenient API that handles retries and buffer resizing automatically.\n\n#### BatchCount\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nCounts the total number of elements in the map using batch lookups.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Only works for hash, LRU-hash, and LPM-trie maps\n- Handles `unix.ENOSPC` errors by doubling the buffer size and retrying (up to 3 times)\n- Returns the total count or an error\n\n**Note:** For maps that don't fit the supported types, returns an error.\n\n#### DeleteAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nDeletes all entries from the map by iterating and deleting individually.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Acquires a write lock\n- Iterates through all keys and deletes each one\n- If cache is enabled, marks all entries as pending deletion before iteration\n- Updates entries in the cache as deletion succeeds or fails\n- Emits a `MapDeleteAll` event to the event buffer if enabled\n\n**Important:** Entries added to the map during this operation may survive the deletion.\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Complete map reset when reloading policies\n- Cleanup before map recreation\n\n#### ClearAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nClears all entries by updating them to their zero values instead of deleting.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Cannot be used with maps that have events buffer or value cache enabled\n- Iterates through all keys and updates each to an empty/zero value\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- When you need to preserve map structure but clear contents\n- Some kernel subsystems require this pattern instead of deletion\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### Simple Iteration with Callbacks\n\n#### DumpWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all map entries and calls the callback for each one.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Opens the map if not already open\n- Acquires a read lock\n- Creates fresh instances of key and value types for each callback invocation\n- Safe to retain the values received in the callback (they're not shared references)\n\n**Returns:** An error if iteration fails.\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := myMap.DumpWithCallback(func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", key, value)\n})\n```\n\n**Important:** Do not call map mutation methods (Update, Delete) from the callback without using `DeleteLocked()`. The lock is held as a read lock, not write.\n\n#### DumpWithCallbackIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback()`, but returns silently if the map doesn't exist.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if the map's pinned file exists first\n- If it doesn't exist, returns `nil` without calling the callback\n- Otherwise behaves like `DumpWithCallback()`\n\n### Per-CPU Iteration\n\n#### DumpPerCPUWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over a per-CPU map and calls the callback with all per-CPU values at once.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- The value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue` interface\n- The callback receives a slice of values (one per CPU)\n- Each callback invocation gets fresh value slices\n\n**Preconditions:**\n- The map must be a per-CPU map type (PerCPUHash, PerCPUArray, etc.)\n- The value type must implement `MapPerCPUValue`\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nerr := myPerCPUMap.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key MapKey, values any) {\n    valuesSlice := values.(*[]MyValue)\n    // Process per-CPU values\n})\n```\n\n### Reliable Iteration with Position Tracking\n\n#### DumpReliablyWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nIterates over a map with advanced tracking to handle concurrent modifications.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Maintains tracking of previously seen keys to recover from iterator resets\n- If a key is deleted during iteration, backtracks to the previous key and resumes from there\n- Caps maximum iterations at 4x the map's max entries to prevent infinite loops\n- Updates the `DumpStats` object with iteration statistics\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Callback function called for each entry\n- `stats`: A `DumpStats` object (created via `NewDumpStats(m)`) for tracking statistics\n\n**Returns:**\n- `nil` if iteration completes successfully\n- `ErrMaxLookup` if the iteration limit is exceeded (indicates a very unstable map)\n- Other errors if iteration fails\n\n**Statistics Provided:**\n- `Lookup`: Total number of key lookups performed\n- `LookupFailed`: Number of failed lookups (key was deleted)\n- `Interrupted`: Number of times iteration was interrupted by deletion\n- `KeyFallback`: Number of times fallback to previous key was used\n- `Completed`: Whether iteration completed successfully\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- When the map is being modified by other processes during iteration\n- Ensuring complete enumeration despite concurrent updates\n\n### Batch Iterator (Modern API)\n\n#### NewBatchIterator\n\n```go\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nCreates a new batch iterator for type-safe batched iteration.\n\n**Type Parameters:**\n- `KT`: Key type (e.g., `MyKey`)\n- `VT`: Value type (e.g., `MyValue`)\n- `KP`: Key pointer type (must be `*KT` and implement `MapKey`)\n- `VP`: Value pointer type (must be `*VT` and implement `MapValue`)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\niter := NewBatchIterator[MyKey, MyValue](myMap)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", *k, *v)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    // Handle iteration error\n}\n```\n\n#### IterateAll\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context,\n    opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\nReturns an iterator Seq2 that yields all key-value pairs from the map.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Uses the eBPF batch API for efficient iteration\n- Handles `unix.ENOSPC` errors by automatically doubling the buffer size and retrying (up to 3 times by default)\n- Respects the provided context (stops iteration if context is cancelled)\n- Resets internal state on each call, allowing reuse of the same iterator\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for cancellation\n- `opts`: Optional configuration for the iteration (batch size, retry count, batch options)\n\n**Returns:** An `iter.Seq2[*KT, *VT]` that can be used in `for k, v := range` loops.\n\n**Behavior on Errors:**\n- If iteration fails due to insufficient buffer (ENOSPC), automatically retries with a larger buffer\n- If retries are exhausted, iteration stops and error is available via `Err()`\n- If other errors occur, iteration stops immediately\n\n**Supported Map Types:**\n- Hash, LRUHash, LPMTrie (only)\n\n#### Batch Iterator Options\n\n##### WithMaxRetries\n\n```go\nfunc WithMaxRetries[...](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nSets the maximum number of buffer expansion retries (default: 3).\n\n##### WithStartingChunkSize\n\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[...](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nSets the initial batch size (default: computed from map size).\n\n##### WithEBPFBatchOpts\n\n```go\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[...](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[...]\n```\n\nPasses through eBPF-specific batch options.\n\n#### Err\n\n```go\nfunc (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\nReturns any error encountered during the previous iteration.\n\n**Note:** Error is reset on subsequent calls to `IterateAll()`.\n\n#### CountAll\n\n```go\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](\n    ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)\n```\n\nHelper function that counts all entries by iterating with the batch iterator.\n\n### Simple Dump to Map\n\n#### Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nDumps the entire map into a `map[string][]string`.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Iterates the map using `DumpWithCallback()`\n- Populates the provided map with string representations of keys and values\n- Multiple values per key are stored as a slice\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Exporting map contents for debugging\n- API responses showing map state\n\n#### DumpIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nLike `Dump()`, but returns silently if the map doesn't exist.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\n### Understanding Pinning\n\nPinning is the mechanism Cilium uses to persist eBPF maps to the filesystem so they survive process restarts. When a map is pinned:\n\n1. It's created in the kernel\n2. A reference to it is stored in the BPF filesystem at a specific path\n3. Subsequent processes can open and reuse the pinned map via its path\n\n### Map Paths\n\n#### BPFFSRoot\n\n```go\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n```\n\nReturns the absolute path to the BPF filesystem mount point.\n\n**Default:** `/sys/fs/bpf` (or `/run/cilium/bpffs` if running in a containerized environment without proper host setup)\n\n**Important:** This function locks the BPFFS root and must be called before any other path-related functions.\n\n#### CiliumPath\n\n```go\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n```\n\nReturns the path to the Cilium object directory within the BPF filesystem.\n\n**Returns:** `{BPFFSRoot()}/cilium`\n\n#### TCGlobalsPath\n\n```go\nfunc TCGlobalsPath() string\n```\n\nReturns the path to the TC (traffic control) globals directory.\n\n**Returns:** `{BPFFSRoot()}/tc/globals`\n\n**Note:** Used for legacy map pin paths.\n\n#### MapPath\n\n```go\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n```\n\nReturns the full filesystem path for a map with the given name.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If running in the Cilium agent, returns `{TCGlobalsPath()}/{name}`\n- Otherwise, queries mount info to find the BPF filesystem location\n\n#### LocalMapName\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\nGenerates a map name that's local to a specific ID (e.g., per-endpoint).\n\n**Returns:** `{name}{id:05d}` (e.g., `mymap00001`)\n\n#### LocalMapPath\n\n```go\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\nReturns the path for a map that's local to a specific ID.\n\n### Map Path Methods\n\n#### Path\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\nReturns the computed path where this map is (or will be) pinned.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- If the path hasn't been set, computes it from the map name\n- Returns an error if the path cannot be computed\n\n**Returns:** The pinned path, or an error.\n\n#### Name\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string\n```\n\nReturns the basename of the map.\n\n### Unpin Operations\n\n#### Unpin\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n```\n\nRemoves the map from the BPF filesystem (unpin operation).\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Gets the pin path\n- Removes the pinned file/directory\n\n**Important:** This does **not** close the map or release kernel resources. If the map is still open in other processes, it remains in the kernel.\n\n#### UnpinIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n```\n\nUnpins the map if it exists, silently succeeding if it doesn't.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Checks if the pinned file exists first\n- Only calls `Unpin()` if it does\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\n### MapKey Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapKey.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String()` for debugging and event logging\n- Must implement `New()` to create fresh instances for iteration\n- Usually a struct with field tags matching eBPF struct layout (e.g., `align` tags)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyKey struct {\n    ID     uint32 `align:\"id\"`\n    Flags  uint8  `align:\"flags\"`\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyKey{ID: %d, Flags: %d}\", k.ID, k.Flags)\n}\n\nfunc (k *MyKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &MyKey{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n    // New must return a pointer to a new MapValue.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must implement `String()` for debugging and event logging\n- Must implement `New()` to create fresh instances for iteration\n- Usually a struct matching eBPF value struct layout\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyValue struct {\n    Count uint64 `align:\"count\"`\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyValue{Count: %d}\", v.Count)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyValue{}\n}\n```\n\n### MapPerCPUValue Interface\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs implementing MapValue.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n**Used for:** Per-CPU maps that store separate values for each CPU.\n\n**Requirements:**\n- Must also implement `MapValue`\n- Must implement `NewSlice()` to create fresh slice instances for iteration\n- The returned slice should be `*[]YourType` where `YourType` implements `MapValue`\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype MyCPUValue struct {\n    CPUData uint64\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyCPUValue) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"MyCPUValue{CPUData: %d}\", v.CPUData)\n}\n\nfunc (v *MyCPUValue) New() MapValue {\n    return &MyCPUValue{}\n}\n\ntype MyCPUValues []MyCPUValue\n\nfunc (v *MyCPUValue) NewSlice() any {\n    return &MyCPUValues{}\n}\n```\n\n### EndpointKey Example\n\nThe `EndpointKey` is a concrete example of a `MapKey` that represents endpoints in Cilium:\n\n```go\nconst (\n    EndpointKeyIPv4 uint8 = 1\n    EndpointKeyIPv6 uint8 = 2\n)\n\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6 `align:\"$union0\"`  // IPv6 (or IPv4 in lowest 4 bytes)\n    Family    uint8      `align:\"family\"`\n    Key       uint8      `align:\"key\"`\n    ClusterID uint16     `align:\"cluster_id\"`\n}\n\nfunc NewEndpointKey(addr netip.Addr, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey {\n    // Constructs an EndpointKey from an IP address\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string {\n    // Provides string representation\n}\n\nfunc (k EndpointKey) New() MapKey {\n    return &EndpointKey{}\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\n### Understanding Events\n\nWhen events buffer is enabled, the map tracks all mutation operations (updates and deletes) in a ring buffer. This is useful for:\n\n- Auditing map changes\n- Streaming changes to external systems\n- Debugging map state changes\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n#### WithEvents\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables the event buffer for this map.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `c.Enabled`: Whether to enable the buffer\n- `c.MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to store (in-memory)\n- `c.TTL`: Time-to-live for events; older events are garbage collected\n\n**Returns:** The map (for chaining).\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nmyMap.WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n    Enabled: true,\n    MaxSize: 10000,\n    TTL: 5 * time.Minute,\n})\n```\n\n### Event Types\n\n#### Action Enum\n\n```go\ntype Action uint8\n\nconst (\n    MapUpdate  Action = iota // Update/Insert operation\n    MapDelete               // Delete operation\n    MapDeleteAll            // Bulk delete operation\n)\n```\n\n### Event Structure\n\n#### Event\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time\n    // (private action field)\n    Key           MapKey\n    Value         MapValue\n    DesiredAction DesiredAction\n    LastError     error\n}\n```\n\n**Fields:**\n- `Timestamp`: When the operation occurred\n- `GetAction()`: Returns the action as a string (\"update\", \"delete\", \"delete-all\")\n- `GetKey()`: Returns the key string representation\n- `GetValue()`: Returns the value string representation (or \"<nil>\" for deletes)\n- `GetLastError()`: Returns any error from the operation\n- `GetDesiredAction()`: Returns the desired action status (OK, Insert, Delete)\n\n### Event Subscription\n\n#### DumpAndSubscribe\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(Event)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(ctx context.Context, callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool) void\n```\n\nDumps existing events and optionally subscribes to future ones.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `ctx`: Context for the subscription (cancel to stop receiving events)\n- `callback`: Function called for each event (existing and future)\n- `follow`: If `true`, continues receiving events; if `false`, only dumps existing\n\n**Behavior:**\n- First, calls the callback with all existing events in the buffer (in order)\n- If `follow` is `true`, subscribes to future events and calls callback for each new one\n- Uses the provided context for lifetime management\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\ndefer cancel()\n\nmyMap.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(event Event) {\n    if event.GetAction() == \"update\" {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Updated: %s = %s\\n\", event.GetKey(), event.GetValue())\n    }\n}, true) // Follow = true for streaming\n\n// Subscription continues until ctx is cancelled\n```\n\n#### IsEventsEnabled\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nReturns whether event buffering is enabled for this map.\n\n### Desired Action Status\n\nThe `DesiredAction` field tracks the state of an entry:\n\n```go\ntype DesiredAction uint8\n\nconst (\n    OK     DesiredAction = iota  // Entry is in sync with kernel\n    Insert                       // Entry needs to be inserted (pending retry)\n    Delete                       // Entry needs to be deleted (pending retry)\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\n### Loading eBPF Collections\n\nThe collection loading API handles loading compiled eBPF ELF files (collections of programs and maps) into the kernel.\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants to substitute in eBPF code\n    Constants any\n\n    // Map renames: map old names to new names\n    MapRenames []map[string]string\n\n    // Maps to substitute (already-open maps)\n    MapReplacements map[string]*Map\n\n    // Objects to keep during reachability pruning\n    Keep *set.Set[string]\n\n    // Path to dump configuration constants\n    ConfigDumpPath string\n}\n```\n\n### LoadAndAssign\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF collection from a spec and assigns programs/maps to fields in a struct.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `logger`: Logger for operations\n- `to`: A struct with fields for eBPF programs and maps (uses `ebpf` struct tags)\n- `spec`: The compiled eBPF collection spec\n- `opts`: Configuration for loading\n\n**Returns:**\n- A commit function to call after programs are attached to kernel hooks\n- An error if loading fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Analyzes struct fields to determine what to load\n- Loads the collection into the kernel\n- Assigns loaded programs and maps to the provided struct\n- Returns a function that must be called after entrypoints are attached (for final pinning)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\ntype Objects struct {\n    ProgIngress *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_to_netdev\"`\n    ProgEgress  *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"cil_from_netdev\"`\n    MapState    *Map          `ebpf:\"cilium_state\"`\n}\n\nobjs := &Objects{}\ncommit, err := LoadAndAssign(logger, objs, spec, nil)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n\n// Attach programs to hooks\n// ...\n\n// Commit pending map pins after attachment\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### LoadCollection\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec,\n    opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads a collection spec into the kernel with advanced options.\n\n**Returns:**\n- The loaded collection\n- A commit function for pending map pins\n- An error if loading fails\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Applies constants to the spec\n- Renames maps as specified\n- Performs reachability analysis to prune unused code\n- Resolves tail call slots\n- Handles incompatible pinned maps by recreating them\n- Returns a commit function to finalize pinning after program attachment\n\n**Important:** The commit function **must** be called after all programs are attached to kernel hooks to ensure pending map pins are finalized.\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Map Creation and CRUD\n\n```go\npackage main\n\nimport (\n    \"fmt\"\n    \"log/slog\"\n\n    \"github.com/cilium/ebpf\"\n    \"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/bpf\"\n)\n\ntype Counter struct {\n    ID uint32 `align:\"id\"`\n}\n\nfunc (c *Counter) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"id=%d\", c.ID)\n}\n\nfunc (c *Counter) New() bpf.MapKey {\n    return &Counter{}\n}\n\ntype Count struct {\n    Value uint64 `align:\"value\"`\n}\n\nfunc (c *Count) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"count=%d\", c.Value)\n}\n\nfunc (c *Count) New() bpf.MapValue {\n    return &Count{}\n}\n\nfunc main() {\n    logger := slog.Default()\n\n    // Initialize BPF filesystem\n    bpf.CheckOrMountFS(logger, \"\")\n\n    // Create a map\n    m := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_counters\",\n        ebpf.Hash,\n        &Counter{},\n        &Count{},\n        1000,\n        0)\n\n    // Open or create the map in the kernel\n    if err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to create map\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n    defer m.Close()\n\n    // Update a value\n    key := &Counter{ID: 42}\n    value := &Count{Value: 100}\n    if err := m.Update(key, value); err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to update\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n\n    // Lookup a value\n    result, err := m.Lookup(key)\n    if err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to lookup\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n    fmt.Printf(\"Result: %v\\n\", result)\n\n    // Delete a value\n    if err := m.Delete(key); err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Failed to delete\", \"error\", err)\n        return\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Iteration with BatchIterator\n\n```go\nfunc dumpMapContents(ctx context.Context, m *bpf.Map) error {\n    iter := bpf.NewBatchIterator[Counter, Count](m)\n\n    for k, v := range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n        fmt.Printf(\"Key: %v, Value: %v\\n\", k, v)\n    }\n\n    if err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n        return fmt.Errorf(\"iteration failed: %w\", err)\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n### Conditional Deletion During Iteration\n\n```go\nfunc deleteExpiredEntries(m *bpf.Map) error {\n    return m.DumpWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n        if isExpired(value) {\n            // Safe to delete within callback using DeleteLocked\n            if err := m.DeleteLocked(key); err != nil {\n                // Log error but continue iteration\n                fmt.Printf(\"Failed to delete: %v\\n\", err)\n            }\n        }\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### Event Subscription\n\n```go\nfunc subscribeToMapChanges(ctx context.Context, m *bpf.Map) {\n    m.DumpAndSubscribe(ctx, func(event bpf.Event) {\n        action := event.GetAction()\n        key := event.GetKey()\n        value := event.GetValue()\n\n        fmt.Printf(\"[%s] %s = %s\\n\", action, key, value)\n\n        if err := event.GetLastError(); err != nil {\n            fmt.Printf(\"  Error: %v\\n\", err)\n        }\n    }, true) // follow=true for streaming\n}\n```\n\n### Per-CPU Map Usage\n\n```go\ntype PerCPUStats struct {\n    PacketCount uint64 `align:\"pkt_count\"`\n}\n\nfunc (s *PerCPUStats) String() string {\n    return fmt.Sprintf(\"pkts=%d\", s.PacketCount)\n}\n\nfunc (s *PerCPUStats) New() bpf.MapValue {\n    return &PerCPUStats{}\n}\n\ntype PerCPUStatsSlice []PerCPUStats\n\nfunc (s *PerCPUStats) NewSlice() any {\n    return &PerCPUStatsSlice{}\n}\n\nfunc dumpPerCPUStats(m *bpf.Map) error {\n    return m.DumpPerCPUWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, values any) {\n        statsSlice := values.(*PerCPUStatsSlice)\n        for cpu, stats := range *statsSlice {\n            fmt.Printf(\"CPU %d: %v\\n\", cpu, stats)\n        }\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### Map with Cache and Error Recovery\n\n```go\nfunc createManagedMap() *bpf.Map {\n    return bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_managed\",\n        ebpf.Hash,\n        &Counter{},\n        &Count{},\n        10000,\n        0).\n        WithCache(). // Enable cache for consistency tracking\n        WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{\n            Enabled: true,\n            MaxSize: 5000,\n            TTL: 10 * time.Minute,\n        })\n}\n```\n\n### Reliable Iteration with Statistics\n\n```go\nfunc dumpReliably(m *bpf.Map) error {\n    stats := bpf.NewDumpStats(m)\n\n    err := m.DumpReliablyWithCallback(func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n        fmt.Printf(\"%v: %v\\n\", key, value)\n    }, stats)\n\n    if err != nil && !errors.Is(err, bpf.ErrMaxLookup) {\n        return err\n    }\n\n    fmt.Printf(\"Lookups: %d, Failed: %d, Interrupted: %d\\n\",\n        stats.Lookup, stats.LookupFailed, stats.Interrupted)\n\n    if stats.Completed {\n        fmt.Println(\"Iteration completed successfully\")\n    }\n\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Concepts\n\n### Cache and Synchronization\n\nWhen `.WithCache()` is enabled:\n\n- All entries updated by userspace are tracked in a local cache\n- Each entry records its desired action (`OK`, `Insert`, `Delete`) and last error\n- On update failure, the cache is marked for synchronization\n- An error resolver controller periodically retries failed operations\n- This ensures eventual consistency between userspace and kernel state\n\n### Pressure Metrics\n\nMaps can be configured to report \"pressure\" (capacity usage):\n\n```go\nm.WithPressureMetric(registry)  // Report with 0% threshold\nm.WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry, 0.8)  // Report when > 80% full\n```\n\nThe pressure metric tracks: `(cache_size / max_entries)`\n\n### Map Registration\n\nMaps are automatically registered and tracked internally for debugging. Use `GetModel()` to retrieve the API representation:\n\n```go\nmodel := m.GetModel()  // Returns *models.BPFMap with cache entries\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Types\n\n- `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist`: Key not found in map\n- `ebpf.ErrMapIncompatible`: Existing map has different attributes\n- `unix.ENOSPC`: Batch lookup buffer too small (auto-retried by BatchIterator)\n- `os.ErrNotExist`: Pinned map file doesn't exist\n- `ErrMaxLookup`: Iteration limit reached (concurrent modifications)\n\n### Best Practices\n\n1. **Always check errors** from `Lookup()` with `errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)`\n2. **Use `SilentDelete()`** for cleanup operations where missing entries are OK\n3. **Call `Close()`** in defer statements to ensure resources are released\n4. **Enable cache** for maps with complex synchronization requirements\n5. **Use `DumpReliablyWithCallback()`** when iterating maps that may be modified concurrently\n6. **Use `BatchIterator`** for efficient iteration of large maps\n\n---\n\n## See Also\n\n- eBPF kernel documentation: https://docs.kernel.org/userspace-api/ebpf/index.html\n- Cilium documentation: https://docs.cilium.io\n- ebpf-go library: https://github.com/cilium/ebpf\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
